Great Expectations


In his note to investors, J.P. Morgan analyst Doug Anmuth breaks down the hiring of Googler Marissa Mayer as CEO. He writes, "We believe Mayer's background as one of Google's earliest engineers and her experience overseeing key products suggests the company will refocus on the user experience and pace of innovation. Importantly, we believe Mayer may also be able to attract more high quality engineering talent to Yahoo!, which we think is needed after several years of strategic and leadership flux. Mayer was with Google for nearly 13 years, joining the company as its 20th employee. Most recently, Mayer was the VP of Location and Local Services where she oversaw Google products including Google Earth, Zagat, Street View, and local search, for desktop and mobile. Prior to her role in Google Local, Mayer managed many of Google's high profile products including Search, Google News, and Gmail." Yahoo! is a tech-first company again? A product company, at the least. Meanwhile, All Things D's Kara Swisher reports that interim CEO Ross Levinsohn is on his way out. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAlzkQnlUXkjbiIFOtbtdrB05saJs4nOsB2CK006v8H43P-HrjqM8yTG9j8jOM_CrIj2ORWfuBgaG_RvubuhaUEzqe_e3FvtzS7NAzmsVNN0xGb6kDxf0kFhRvnGWNtJhnXSvMAo8xWroUZQNm-vCTLvw4ZJNvcm0eJO8WWhNP_74sv4pfRkt06VhJoce1FtT6QBoo_H5Oj6lJSGKib63bKs>  Forrester's Shar VanBoskirk doesn't like <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAkfLdubi2PCTo5oE7I2B_OmHH2wvB4jRF78O2dzLwRtKs2huuWuuK4qUQrlV5i2_gfQ-LjS74RhcYb6XSjTuAV7Cji_9T6KYOGfhUKLpHXP71yykoWuUFeCR0tczIeBXK9ZuJ0KxckdK7cgcX3INN5amBhEUrlrtTmxUJoiJNvZuxe3lITTawaL_H_RwcwXYFs=>  the new CEO choice. And, read assorted Googlers reaction on Marketing Land. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAmo2Jir7GDKLTcTSYx3rNX79JdxTF_eN8S9STYHWfzEuY_jITSE6qRUagxxdxXAgwl78TSQaTZ6L-sNZZg0kL4viFT5lE1wwTEUXDf0iRt7PQZ4KP3JHzky2d7Sd75thMXLDE6qIcVzoTzS-VFY2t94PSBE0INW5CJ-qE0DHwzdNrH5UsuLuLf6bATd1vtFK_hDXSziXj6gjg==>  


Future Yield


It's 2020. Your hovercraft is pulled over at the side of the new galactic interstate with a punctured fuel cell. You wonder, "How are my ads monetizing today?" Adchemy CEO Murthy Nukala gives four ways ads will be a-monetizing in an article on TechCrunch. The first: "Entertainment will either be monetized by the content itself (e.g., paying for a game, or for a subscription to watch a show), and/or by advertising that will be broadcast in nature. Social ads on Facebook may not drive response as much as other online channels, but Facebook's wide reach and high traffic will make it a natural venue for brand-awareness campaigns (e.g., opening night for a blockbuster movie)." Read 'em all. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAkyWzYUPiECUKuOuD0vFg4WwmWnSljkSPvoDPrf8AU-2lRsPAHc1iNIvJ3gLlO8UlK0V1yVeCLwS23DKM-xSindetov3cR7j7bWjf7j9981VBpuuM0Sv9mFscEBid75VoE31X2x9_-wm1Px4bVImBzA4uSVzpd7oz1mNlN9yMJsWA==>  


Going Mobile


Describing its May 2012 acquisition of Mobsmith as a precursor to its foray into mobile ads, sell-side platform Rubicon Project announced yesterday REVV for Mobile, "which enables publishers to sell mobile ad inventory through both direct and indirect sales channels." The company adds, "REVV for Mobile is available immediately to U.S. publishers, and will be available to the international market in September 2012." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAkIcBf7GX76bs1PV0VKlLrgkAzhltJFoX0-8JyOAcT5o8d42gBvZn8awWR6oKdFcWpsCpFBUhTM1FfhZhURHOPhyTjb7nkNQrxiFGye76NA4bvJkGiWEIwrFfs_ajFDGeeWqi0VBge54C9cVkUMPL10yaG2fc-iPF8MHgCGlvqJ5cfdJAIvYCyk>  


It's The Human


In a think piece on ClickZ, GroupNext exec Chris Copeland emphasizes the importance of the human in charge of a digital strategy. He writes,"Technology is an important part of the digital business. The tools utilized daily for search, display, social media, and every other channel are a key piece of the successes and failures of the industry. But a tool left in the hands of someone unable to understand that everyone has tools is a waste." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAmWx1ZUddHlQJRb98RdN-Qb1BnNN5PJRZVlQvTQFQ3dvEaCfnGc7pfA4BbBfjVDOImKH5oyzi0L9uI8xPxFtrSIBNB2DbcJct7aceuds1e7nLwITJ7urKEWHwfqOngkPOZBhKk9etW2QMuCjK5M3mbVSnvLgk6GhKwG37SqBfYqpyhETOiOw7kfM86IS727g7IRjKmLY5cdWXazZf6WN6AsJeOURAV2r-E=>  


"Rebate" Debate Redux


Talk of media rebates and "kickbacks" for agencies are bound to worry advertisers, but is it a bogeyman issue? Google and Vivaki were once alleged to have done it, as detailed by TechCrunch in 2010 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAmWPEwsUzxZ57ONKnwQmUoh6P-tEcdVPrgvTpfDDCbHCMSkiyCgEJoJeZMe-n4Jx4Ilvy9qszqbe9T3Ckd_bUabZ9We-LvikXjHXU1MNoSotW-VneIaJMOZF30RrcHXeR12RhaF6rJ1gE_wwihipc-jTPVNGpq4DnM=> . (Both denied it at the time.) A new ANA survey examines the rebate specter and finds growing awareness among U.S. advertisers. Real examples are harder to come by. AdAge's Jack Neff makes a call and learns, "One senior media-agency executive who asked not to be identified said he hasn't seen any rebates being offered and certainly hasn't asked for them, but couldn't comment on what others may be doing." To be safe, the ANA is urging contractual language. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAlGieehLqlSQcB1El2Uu2_SiZ8R-py6VPqbrS53N8svvMPsP0M5zQpXdnV-BPdRHEdSJtrhqTyXq9Q3X9_V9oVE2l2t-75lxayPMMo1RFfLQNUOzH3fjdDYdVO7s-NVE_1tnJoW70gX7G_Ot17finiNPf82C2l8VC5BGP2Ii-az550FEh6yt5FKfE9EGLbVdPuchdlKMAsR6A==>  


High Touch Ads


Users of tablets and smartphones both interact heavily with ads, says a new IAB study. The difference between them, notes TechCrunch's Ingrid Lunden, has to do with content use patterns. "As we've seen from other tablet research, people are more likely to be using their tablets to read and consume entertainment media for longer periods of time, while smartphones are about short bursts of use." On a smartphone? Read the post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAkp3dlt8fsDQx59Om20DYv66bgv6isxoWxTzcP2TpG9cZFbrq0akML-g6JyqoDTCQz7ULSaVn3DLeJrYYWYg__GQeJOjKIhIj4L_HR159TWtzh0D-RuV-H2yfJpZd3fsZpH_dtFeBruEzJirZnix6dHebvm7BTpCU9jhVaGXZ_DWduOrsr4Wy4RSihTd61p1WPjcLQQTDLK--gyypM3VzeMTwrLm1UICtWSbtZzJLpg8px3VkkJE8zCtQqYCxlCLIgLBRTkGM86I3-q62gNreJaperBekOtLPeuEKImhedWjzL5B0EJ8os5BOAkKgyIYGG-60MTUEkYEn5a3ujLZ9NZJBytz3jzjyqOvYfVJryp5QPPc0T8TOkKuiZKE2zV9Ss=> . Targeting Olympians


Here's a new angle on a B2B marketing campaign. CAPTCHA ad network Solve Media says it has decided to emphasize its targeting capabilities by sponsoring Olympic athletes. From the release, "the company's capabilities align closely to both [U.S. weightlifter Sarah Robles and archer Brady Ellison]'s abilities -- accomplishing massive lift and precise targeting. (...) On a mission to become the best in the world, Sarah, Brady and Solve Media make a strong team." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012TlHsj0hbAkjp1MwBMPLthCBXdM2xka0Nrq-pL27ZFCflt0Kkmu3UuJOj7HOITPmMkZHC147InmZMuHb_pWH9to85ly6Meh1a1Vb0XW1ND2DbArsLPwBxB03efO8U8ZavGf9__jXYCaciAvInF3EWKCY4qp40QyzKj9RQOaem6TYhh4S03qiB0eAEn66AFGnmIniiQYVDjpCQKqyzK2MsDM9Nqb-0i09ZluR2tgo6xyCuhG1yzthxdShebq2pvQ_4dc13bYXkpI=>  Who will be the first ad tech company to sponsor a New Year's Day bowl game?

Clicks Matter And Don't


A new study from Jumptap finds that clickthrough rate is not necessarily an indicator of good or bad performance. From the release: "Jumptap compared data from 10 major gaming advertisers in May and found that a campaign could have a very low CTR but a high conversion rate, or a high CTR and a low conversion rate." What's a marketer to do? Or a mobile publisher for that matter? Read the release, and get the study <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7p81LJkdnBqdFmGsFFYeNxN0_lxQ_78YN3-90m_beDXEqmlcovFK0ZzPl232cYbwe0_S6X8HR_BOZaziSE-bzYimnIUNO0R9WidQcXpUXKNzYLsUe3sksEmUmTLt6rk25LgFShNytFx4oL_6wNjEpvp2KQkl4QkPG_AOpmijQMbMFlCEyfZO4CKIYr3L0PPGktKgJky7DCIOhpGchyRvFmXOr22gcGGzVLDSYb2RRf3n4ts7yCpHpl2d61xOLl5anEP7HWVEj0VIA==> . 


IBM And Social


On DM News, Nicole Spector writes that the latest update to IBM's Customer Experience Suite aims at "new enterprise demands due to consumer upticks in mobile and social media adoption." She quotes IBM's Lisa Lucadamo Jarrett who says, "Owned social communities can now be connected to external social networks like Facebook." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7riQTZ21B6WNdVdPsQ9W-17EPJ5OGQnyCDyGt_7EgtQmSJ2g3WOEbq5K4ixuSZDJCcWkd9dc0JE7haPYCiZHChr1Pub4XTmpUYLOFZFDPf0EMjKm7V_R6BvoPm0PAJX9g5cbBztPghTm_VNsmqHx2lAR4eRNw3AVYo8GrDxH-_8uWuP5HHttZJl> . And, read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7rCBJF3B-5p8i2nIdl80EN4DJodI-_elekMd04gibYFlfLXnhTX1iRlt0Mp8hc7OszBYDMyyH7xM7yEAWB1KtAR6H5iroaJRSaPTTrImOqbubCfd3UxhKoGEDbg7ej8AFBulzQAbxqcAm0YEKK2s8POfy4j5nCRWL4ZDrcLST2E9x5uNAEAxtXixFUBNTNPSme_9OLVbBhatBr-FeUylf7p> . It will be interesting to see if IBM acquires or creates a paid media tool to "pour" through a product such as this. 


RTB Publisher


On MediaPost, CEO Skip Brand of Martini Media claims that real-time bidding (RTB) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7qgJB5hcf9juSbqdMKHV6ZuBB_CmvaP9Fotovp2c3kflrdht-4GqQKrUcACXuGNb6A_sV-wcLIc-KJcJ1owIc1-kuxSKbVMDehYzKcdrLYHrObjtiGGUvTji-H_hC_9WZvbLkg6McgokGaF29Oc3vtXmi40vawNfjcdWRGOHz5La7pVEMvAeSQUDfoWpwEoBzw=>  has a huge upside for publishers and includes a list of five types of data points which are of value to publishers in an RTB environment including, "Brand lift: If you don't think brand lift is important, I need to ask you to go no further than Nielsen's purchase of Vizu <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7qMHJT8Zmqj5BgAC0aIkhqu0TNXQ3PTK3hu8yuhGisQ1iV1hwnlxIcTmsq1yHhaxfhxVIFJtOhAE3pWfRqaUMaj4JlKG7uFaS90a5JWb50XLpaunQERx_YbEE9qf3Bp-1j3aUJsfxcfl-JKXF3NhRBKRm2O4-ASrfA=>  on July 2. Arguably the biggest media measurement company in the world purchased a small company that makes it its business to map digital marketing efforts to traditional brand metrics." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7qxCMadXq-xQviM_5Mk5JXW2fwBXoCAGAYkMbhsWXFaaMo_9Twd8ZCdHLcyJra7Y-AYTuLQEJEt92pyG2Ot_Xd7o8h081kYApoQI37yBIf6ukCPmyzTXeLzldf2P4hJmWzf8sR70JPmVXTC7FxNgDmwReK_xy8Js7RfruvULes5xf-RcRqdbZk4>  


I Want My RTB


Alex White, GM of Data and Trading at MediaMind, spreads the love on iMedia Connection and says that changes in the AppNexus platform signifies, in part, real-time bidding (RTB) is maturing. White writes, "When the AppNexus Platform opened up to a plug-and-play model earlier this year, it was a huge shift in how we've previously thought about online display buying. Suddenly, buyers no longer had to negotiate separate deals with vendors for access to targeting and data tools that improve RTB performance and efficiency. They could simply turn on different tools within an open platform and monitor the results to find the perfect mix of targeting technologies." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7qrDaTnX4vtvMxtTiptJzUul411nTZkInmvhi9Bl8YiupeIwx1Q6xzOOUHNnGRzPir9G1KDpqZLzmD37LKnn_g-FBVQ-m2-p5px1XKRHvFZs5d2xn3PiGEM4azVwWsjO9ITzkthUBCObQ==>  


Can You Pick Up, Please?


Responding on his personal blog to a NY Times article <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7rWZM3XJpwCbMkP4jqu1JNW1IkKFn38Li9xnhNUUvci1ilrd8LdkE_PvKPqHFlNFLENFsn76XFl-XNtwN3GtfHSyRecZTgaG_pwTO1K03LcneIT55qePUP1_iK8tuAkpFQG4q0XxL6nwsbbfMjy1oBAnT20oZE1_lTHSgjnRyGbRmewRvN4RpjN_JDF4d3wESBeLk9yLIfj7A==>  that suggested tech companies aren't interested in answering the phone, venture capital maven Mark Suster says it's more about turning the customer into the product. Audience buying is at the center of it as he explains: "Google, Facebook & Twitter all provide free services to end users and we eat them up. But they make the overwhelming majority of their money from advertising. They are selling audiences to advertisers. They are packaging you up into demographic and psychographic audiences - all the better to be purchased by brands trying to reach large niche audiences. They offer targeting tools for geographies, married people, parents, income levels, political affiliation - everything." People are ads. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7pUz49T-AfKoz45qj39oHM8LhZHdPIIJfxfTjzWb39MRIyM00zikaElFo2ESYSIP_QRQ3EB0L0VZ8IKHQVQuKPTyIuwYwXaQ8pJIcd-AJ5diceTAneyn6Az337oMW-qVa4WIpiC2O0CKDc28OOmQ54AsuuPWopVCdqyK8aZ4D-A8m8SMjS2H1fFDqccbM466xEkpqROUpmbIQLk3LmceZ9UK6dwFjfI6KtPQ3IFUW6ALA==> . 


Ad Tech And Healthcare


In a post on his personal blog, Nat Turner, the former CEO of Invite Media who is busy on a new healthcare-related startup, sees a connection between the risk shifting in online ad tech between advertisers and publishers, and the healthcare industry. He writes, " If you look ad ad-tech, over the last 15 years there has also been a shift of risk from publishers to advertisers. (...) Then, companies like Ad.com and others popped up (...) who allowed advertisers to pay out on CPA and thus pay for media only when that media generates a sale for them. That created a full risk shift to the publisher, which made them accountable for the performance of the media and in theory aligned the industry." What it all means. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SIycXFT3P7qMXd8NTE410NnJiYy0bGqu9aI9BzXx9wzhGdCnZB8O4LL8ecDPCMHPcR1Vxsx4K1TIEUHU5yH1nYsE-Hdl_xc5HU5_SruA_oMRapDpTOyiOh215WW55K3XN-oFgTce0Ys=>

Marketing Tech M&A


Investment banker David Clark discusses ad tech trends in a Jordan Edmiston 'Client Briefing'. He draws a distinction between marketing tech and ad tech, and writes, "Equally interesting to observe are the new 'industry' participants from outside the ad tech sector that are getting pulled closer to the digital event horizon. In terms of M&A activity, what we're seeing is ad tech M&A giving way to 'marketing technology' M&A. There is a notable cooling down of M&A in the ad tech categories of search and display services and tools, while M&A activity has heated up in marketing infrastructure, particularly for technology solutions that address the needs of global brand marketers and premium publishers (including ecommerce brands that operate as marketer and publisher alike)." Read more (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD1D3Oh2XUcrUa4qz_Wsx744a6I3qb_q0Ikg5IsU3DHJKZVArAyZNmG4Gk7lPKwe5uN53_wXswOz6Ur4u7uZG5jlMviSVtODr5bCJGNwf1eKmiBu47DYIAa_O6PNeUQ6BKLNMlFoLZp8KPGwduxPRqaTxua_MY75y4I_vEJxS-OwwQ==> . 


Automated Selling


In Adweek, Mike Shields follows up on a WSJ report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD1cMGvkiYqiRivwp_-4a0XcebbrADNwIDKSO8cIiwwzjVTNyPHpW9ff-bOsXdDXaB6si6bE59hKcyYV_dtu4awvdjQKxSLibs0OTEsCbo8JJ1lyQrh17o3W7KtRqac5JAwSECzDaEmA_AEXZLzX22FVV6az0zfPA3qwqMus4u0EOmvLaS8tU5oM>  that Microsoft Advertising is going through a round of layoffs and says, "According to sources, Microsoft has completely eliminated its mobile advertising team, with the exception of Jeff Plaisted, director of sales and strategy, mobile & Skype Advertising (perhaps indicated that Skype is about to take on a more prominent role in Microsoft's ad strategy)." Shields hears others in the branded entertainment group are getting the pick slip as the moves signal Microsoft Advertising is pinning its future on automated selling. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD2789sJZg5mMPNauBRdRhllWqzEbekcniAuB2xB4i70g5Z8uvA9q6mZMiL76KUtcuBkFiFvCLfEj5Th6sY9TIo9QeLhKwFV3ei6AOCR0DIxaVVdUzg7xhrJarTRFxebHq62uY7-mL0JMzwuOyUiY7OQ8vVsR4vli5sLaY4wiIEGP-BUkr9dpaoo9llmw4HkhMWtDQjIjuhZpMLd1Z9upcZ0> . 


Automated Buying


Cotton Delo reports in Ad Age that Facebook ad buying partners are being given access to new self-serve buying capabilities. Delo writes, "Starting today, Facebook will make premium inventory available through its self-serve Power Editor tool and to third-party Facebook ad sellers like Blinq Media, TBG Digital and AdParlor. These 'premium ads' are the ones that appear on the right rail of a user's news feed as opposed to a users' profile page. It's considered prime ad real estate because that's where users spend most of their time." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD1EfJSS7ZXCAbshFSsV4aOFC1bjHJq5cNp_4A3dMy4wMTLmVZTMYjS2sVrwwO44V6voJcyOjpM7LSCc4ApLnDQnGkTqXwlputonFU0tmSJBxmmXkYSXGlM95TmenFJ-MvZ4_GQ9w099IqDJaFjjWOCuEhvj_25lONUyk-CacGoRyeoe4bFjsef0Aet2L8V8cxylY3Uk12iwZw==> 


Tracking CPCs


Marin Software has culled industry observations from its clients' data in its Q2 2012 advertising report. A CPC observation: "Compared to ads shown on desktop and laptop computers, paid search ads on tablet devices continue to show favorable performance levels. The cost per click (CPC) for paid search ads run on tablets is 18 percent lower than that of ads run on computers. Also, the click-through rate (CTR) for paid search ads on tablets is 42 percent higher than ads appearing on computers." Good news for Google overall, according to Marin data, as CPCs were flat as opposed to Q1 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD1Vlhw8R6dwz1iDuJ1UQtZExeUcjn7M_j9HNrIqu0TDzzuCm18Q37zz2kVZzv4PdGSIYpHlO2lyPBi9U-LHZnC0F9ld0D9hNDIgQ9JTCNwA_0AqcTTJITq0WfoKlF_lzkzCJeTmMngZKXAkJ1oOjiC6wGsFM6lICoTqg-ONIeJv_eC_mqlhBatPveWS_aolgA2vdqx2NaMgp1YItvpW8DTVRNCTqN0O35AZc1WBoK1b_g==>  when they were declining. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD3wdcMqXZjuGIGPrn8y04O3KdqHeraD7yOo8vGvqggukAh1JO3Ym1getsRKiTnvl0BiAVrbH1i8R62p4ZADyRIepKqGaNoaLTH2BhRTGI4u8CS83mAJU1T49a_qZOmPwKP4iHflg53-a6SpNEvPwCOk4wHdZMUSRj5Gv8pTHQfOaEgwBWeQLFgU4P2Nvlli09nnuDsuAPaJOXvhgAdrWWKRDuqbGTJlA4Y=> . And, download the report (pay with some PII) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD2JOvF0XTvJfNE9lvoAOWOg0OTnnwlbyGhOsnqZvlYu0mZd1ynIS_LWj19n51JIPchNbTQzea-b0hjopjByjXU3lp89q6x0sBQWlz49VxbdLlwUXc-dMdcPv6ap-SRIr8rVMVRvy3uhJ9BdQygDX33kBsQZd6L-K2NWJRTVJFwKLHEAJu9-Oq7ZuzvWEX7TRyHgaswOW_UPGvyoRh5TDJNN5IwlSCa3NOHXANiUAZsdMCLysFgZVuS6vmxxD2lkCpIqHiwAX2nJN21az_aH7826Q9nQCK5bxA8=> . 


Being Public


On The Motley Fool, Dan Newman looks at recent IPOs including that of mobile ad network Millennial Media whose value has been cut in half since it went public. Newman writes, "It seems that initial public offerings give retail investors like you and me a chance to buy into hype but fail to produce solid returns. But is that just anecdotal evidence? Are the number who get burned by IPOs just more vocal than those who win big? Unfortunately, no." He sees venture-backed companies as a red flag. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD0y8qrppkCwtrkEZSLoERBfnh1kMp-8XAwO1HU3Z7pl4lizFc_pFDZ2TC5YzYKF6wI6IywFZksYwjzSSD5EaTAODQ73QY0WnRDW1_sUPhLxfdW7MMW3jvVhll9bVR5O1WiOjoBPMp1QotHpGvscKnFrbPZBVSPVyy2ATvsVEuMTKThn4BotXQhr> . The fact remains, these companies were able to corral a bunch of cash in an IPO for use in growing their businesses. 


CPG Eye Tracking


There are lots of ways a test-and-learn mindset can influence retail experiences. WSJ shines a light on one of them in a story about CPG marketers' use of retina tracking in simulated store environments. "Kimberly-Clark's researchers used computer screens outfitted with retina-tracking cameras when testing the newest packaging for its Viva paper towels in 2009... Their goal was to find which designs got noticed in the first 10 seconds a shopper looked at a shelf." Real-world creative optimization! Read it (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD3mxIWs28YcT2eSDu2a021OXqFsLljydiy1m7ZAkk7d0nATe3sEM3heDSanY5Tl2A3ozw_zDt7MTrZL_1dUb0hqkFmhmUeJ8pVAKUDBgaiky45zHzoxwk4vSlAkSBYCVpabkucuWD9NpJy2j_8mf8zZw5yfHTC8syWr23iPEHvD6TEaCup-F6clLsvFut0-2rbWMmW66fYbFrmBjB3dBBKZmDgZJOSMG9E=>  


Pinterest Buying


Are brands audience buying on Pinterest? Well.... seems like it's still a branded-content play- as Kellogg's brand-man-about-town Bob Arnold says, "While most of our brands are not in the recipe category, there are some - like Rice Krispies - that are. And for them Pinterest is really logical. Right now, Pinterest is really about branding and awareness around product information and recipes." Read more on Digiday. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD26kz-LUA7wkkiQf1JukVthG4LBf7H_Bu6mFaceQapZt1H0DgN-J_aH5ZW0sjwRGOH2RzxY1w9-T2azRcK9PQ_k3NR7BPQ36Pr8NAd6LYqVKYqe2Gl0bF4p2e8hrLWn1hO7ga_kAmxxSoJOYTce1tl_0vhxBq-o9kE=>  


Ads In The Search Box


Google is pushing search-as-you-Type to AdWords customers with e-commerce sites. It claims the predictive suggestions will move visitors to merchant product pages faster and create a smoother flow from intent to purchase. From the Inside AdWords blog, "The Search As You Type pilot is available to US-based AdWords advertisers for free, up to 25 million searches annually, after which licensing fees would apply." Read the post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD1k7rNbUe1HbH-LRWlRhtJGR_VX-se3WkC16s_-Bk2fxayct8GtjJGG8dKoby9NCHZ1_NQX7hACqueFf_ceT2WpMq6P2_Ez0A6WWO9brs_El8FZZis3rp42_a-CybeWIdQtlyt1ONmYIbuUZ4rUdcsmBl-AudgrDQTHOyqLxF5FZIcSzRgkfaka>  


Data Pulpit


BlueKai CEO Omar Tawakol makes an appearance on Huffington Post touting something he calls, "data activation," a concept which he believes goes beyond addressable display solutions. He writes, "Banners are not the be-all, end-all of digital marketing. In many cases they are not even the centerpiece of your brand's marketing efforts. Banners are one aspect of what you do, and they should be informed by data, but you should also select a partner that will allow you to port that data to multiple places." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD1uQ9T-l8W5KnhaAclaIOVUwV7ig786Ia8NRmjzBNkX_Lh8przCG15zHv05W8I--RmuvgWDbwgIlUtpOa0xgCOa2yPChU3Z0E0LJ_WPdezCCoWpfaSCWO4Zlpaf716VPc1rQSnyyzv0Bz-XGESISd8ooeuHN69LVoLfxNdwhMf4ouxxZV5NovBvp6vnHt7hdbs=>  


About Your Landing Page


Ecommerce web page/site optimizer Monetate provides a few tips on the Shop.org blog for retailers. Did you know... "Dynamic product badging is a highly effective tactic that most merchandisers still aren't using. It involves dynamically rendering badges or text on top of your existing product images. The idea is to highlight important product attributes, such as whether an item is 'New,' a 'Top Seller,' 'Staff Pick,' or 'Just for You.'" The secret sauce is in the messaging. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001B87T0Me3KD0ryOnQrC8467emrbDk5caDJJxJY-z-1FocNmBs1QJACB1OLJQg5QdPER5rMqhEyG2n6XF4yDMSNVswwV6EeMF4KY_g0dr6wvZ5iDxqTw0HoAbjtC_9GL8YaXccSsz1OxIiNkSDGowNbaPN0Ya1ZbJRxI_1V96XDfzVD_8w8JozCglfqfs2qycdZWBu8tl4W0ZiJcZK11g1gQwKKbU12G8XVYmu6KRDhVY=>

Ning Gets Glammed


Almost a year after women's lifestyle blog network Glam Media bought white label social network tool Ning, the two are fully integrating. Techcrunch's Anthony Ha reports <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB4QI_yhVWJ06jUc4crsTO5Qkre-dHjsNG4zlIEIBzwz-Ll6rAlOO1SbN0ChxYs512hhRMIglvjlN0gNsHAUkoOBYweq0j8-lfQO0z8mGLB2wgun2FdjSom4y7CEQ0NYEd7T_AZ-Xta2Hw==>  that the benefits will be immediately felt by the social net communities created with Ning, as they'll be able to take advantage of Glam's ad network. Those sites previously had to handle ad serving on their own. Ads on Ning sites will now be powered by Glam Social, which has been around for two years and was intended to help broaden Glam's reach to individuals' sites in addition to larger and mid-size publishers. Glam claims that Ning is getting 50 million uniques a month as the service is used to create 2,000 new social nets every 30 days. In addition to expanding its overall ad reach, the new social nets could also help produce a more comprehensive vertical ad strategy. Read the release, too <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB7TdRFXFsg7QdeCwEjbNEC-0aqqtmEPiG2BKMOkOjWDR3nFFUMBPToMcVgizip05UJh0F_dn8GnRB6BFBTIfjrgpp9Q0t-Kw3eCcvsYdtXnRtCta3-SmKBnwZyoB1dNmf1A9rt8kwjqS57Tpbt2vu0pavL4UsttEg5x_Veh9sYivA2bdU8Z1pR4xei82VxbQNjf5jrUJXiXVycgGprLmZ45LBD8LBTuH55f3aMe0O2dpfXt5mGm6406> . 


Twitter, The Anti-Facebook


Twitter CEO Dick Costolo tends to define his company against the Facebook grain. He tells the LA Times Twitter will use its significant cash reserves to power its platform and biz goals. "We are going to remain private as long as we want," he says. "I like being private for all sorts of reasons." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB7xVWGUu3kUb02Tyfn-gN4pTStVwlw5CIWalMfb6dPKn9EPKGdIR2BkWlnMV9dTgf6aQC_CT4tUyJcMDZ-5gzIjBPqVHmeAYS1MKhewnSOJ1amkTlOfMRqDDj2IQFa2_VWECAZZVwhQOX4ZuSerZuae_5xrJhcg-AaG9I-JQ0AqRejUy0mzmyOi6m0VtCzD5CGApXIAAwXuu-8Rz-cs5HUQ>  Meanwhile Gerry Shih asks in a Reuters analysis, "Is Twitter building [an] ad business at expense of innovation?" The question is motivated by stricter guidelines placed on developers and other parties, including LinkedIn. "Greater control makes it easier for Twitter to sell advertising against its content -- the media industry's traditional proposition." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB7nvwUO1qZCEyJ47yaLn2A9Izz-HkodcFSp07u1fUd7EL340Jexyf8DJQ7o_giqaVwcZYRINQadzK-YC3PVhSemGMyMXE1e9sib9A-BYauqcAArjDSHproVWBDcNaOHp7HDDH9smIYYT16TUII7t4St-pL_wFhvom-umMx84EGoPBtB1ccaWx5YM5JlptL7tiJ7zWoGLmTWsA2nJfK9Q44ToEYpeUIrrt1P-Of_OYQvb6HJ7p5ErCxN4zyzlMdNsPDkZcH7Gq3C6PqYkCiQMnJUJJy5QpbQvY64694Xy3vtJlrKhSR0Uzc9hqogjBRn72QlBCyeOvDbW9B4Czmm_pBhEy_S9-E5JR4=>  Finally, AllThingsD's Peter Kafka shares a Twitter sales deck geared to one client who shall remain nameless. The important takeaway here is that Twitter sales remain high-touch and low-targeting. For instance a vaunted feature called "enhanced interest" targeting has yet to launch. See the slides. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB4gtPLR31bXdMAGx0FlegLjuPAnDcOMroXS12Hk8_HECzARANBOSnPu2VVnJU1d_fGK6UyNGjCUtWVOh9QP7BeeDJmSWeawTr3fUcvm4xHsBV2ZC8Drdy7RjiByCDsB_lY9h9ca12TT6KgDdErMNzYd9ZZFpmMyGZAMiTEFbqS3bKhcRfmqnKxY>  


Mobile Ads More Portable


The Interactive Advertising Bureau has spent a lot more time trying to streamline the ad units for mobile advertising for several years now, and the latest effort represents a worthwhile step toward its ultimate goal: making the often smaller screens for mobile devices a more attractive platform for premium brand advertising. "The Mobile Rich-media Ad Interface Definitions," or MRAID 1.0, as the new standards are called, are aimed at helping agencies run creative across apps from different publishers, rather than needing to re-write the programming behind their ad creative several times for a single campaign -- a major hurdle for marketers, who are reluctant to spend more time and money on mobile, which still needs to prove its scalability. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB5k3H12j2rYMq_DO9F9lQRqXLtevl3o-ndlTX6IjOkIvCdo9P455Hvf-7UukqSuH5tImV7JhOh5UBPLPHgrT1xK3Cp_0DDuRhJKEkoAE9z3QCIjiprj4w0nPHKYWzYEUlF2trN5-xsXgf7rzNOit_0vnQadJNJzr1x2lkUCzJzt_gnfhlbGPuFwmCxcIDgkcB6Ij3uVcmVponMTpS_7f5l9>  


Retargeting Funds


Proving that retargeting remains a compelling business to be in, ad retargeter AdRoll, which serves the long and mid-tail with its cross-exchange, self-serve retargeting tech, announced that it has picked up $15 million in new funding (that's $19 million total in fundraising says Crunchbase <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB7pnc70LlMzxaDoezhmIX-ifPECf7RbpIoYSwi4uZfopV_Ij5znf5nHiDqS13S6Sih3HI9N2E4wN-7mDbPMh0P_MAG4J_uRgkjm2Jt5frfAK2oalkCwyIBPd57m9XQhPDL2fYKEahSy-0T2P6mBZ9uK> ). According to the release, "AdRoll will grow the team into their 24,000 square-foot downtown San Francisco headquarters and open new domestic and international offices." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB7w3hiNRtvQvYF9kl_KCdRuQK1ZV_1-M28ONZqlPHIPfMEqqUJ14UjMDKQNgFDF35HXxjezTNKIkAxFUIqpcf3IUqxlR9GkJry-X_hrUesjINrJxqjLWQTeiDHzsChvG1CKybwuVAFu_nmcs_3TB88TxzWnMP9ehZeisCpE--jsGbaaOTUarsMrHN1s2gTVXZM3sGQo8n1mYCa0bkn2HEb_UQcojCg0X7g=>  


Make Measurement


Nielsen wants to establish more thought leadership in measurement and has established the new Nielsen Innovation Lab. MediaPost's Joe Mandese quotes Nielsen exec Scott McKinley that "the ultimate goal would be to achieve Madison Avenue's long-term 'holy grail <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB7EyYeUj_mc7CMM_nHPl2TpAKF9x3FahN2xuYsKjFv2ycS0cL_W1Ac8xqlcMbLnpFqqnl1lnFTVtw_TWGcfaN5b-JlyJ5_4BNckkwlspiQE_v6pTJZngS-ALbdI72VQUSg-eWr-z7F0lYUkk01rZ7zKJHeBsRCmXTxyDlkhJoORK4NALyDg24Duu9Yt1bCv4l8=> ' of 'understanding the true value' of advertising, including how it impacts the short- and long-term perceptions and behaviors of consumers." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB4-9nwWinxeEhUE5SUYGY7LXD4eT0ZAy-irGzOe8RZ8rvjD_wmcKO35F62CqO_rAMRXiL9hxpW8aXMi12T8q67ug9HUxVaE4khzov-BUc_J48EUpmJBAaaTUZhQj6XzOpE2P-RyOl6iiTsD142SEmcuKnDTGWOHAHkFESqKJzbvBuag-ldrynk9G7Pbw-PQw5jniYt5JO0_MYeAt6otkeFTdB2ygsQnOhw=>  


OOH Addressability


From the out-of-home channel, Verifone will provide a payment for taxi systems in Washington, D.C... AND they'll get to advertise and provide content to taxi passengers. Syncing ads with payment system data and a location overlay would seem to be pretty powerful. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB7NMwnBPz6QPqHutZw8bAp6g4rTpXrAhuZLRQGeF_f_KBaLYebT9MJfPIbELnl9xYwDGJGwITcTYKRoH0eM79HjQn_DsuS723Y4g-5msykuBhdHj2GAJZRqfazhT3zK_yzZXJ1T_YTjQSXFMtrCgmWk>  


Algorithmic Attribution


That's because it's hard, says Brad Terrell writing for ClickZ. Among the obstacles to doing it the correct way are complex tech requirements, talent scarcity, and moving KPI targets. Oh yeah, and missing data. "It's difficult to get the marketing data required for attribution out of the social media, search properties, and digital devices that consume much of our attention, and this creates significant blind spots for attribution analysis." Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001g6SJQr85DB4u7M7Riv6yliFJ52RHUkXScZa7_1JUure4tNF7hiR3De8OW_VMw8rSJEOmh9A3EVEP54a8fDNJvPyFWhRk-nCNbHa2_UCv8RWudGmLnbn5R7wiN4b81E8w2hupqlX9S86dzumvu6N3Kf_np6My8Q7NO92X_-ZQZxY9OfrTbl8bBatk_ntO3T_K>

Google, FTC Search For Settlement


Google and the Federal Trade Commission are said to be hammering out an acceptable fine so they can end their dispute over whether the search giant misrepresented its privacy practices to consumers, the WSJ's Julia Angwin reports. "The amount will likely be around $22 million -- one of the largest fines the FTC has handed down, but a cost that Google will hardly feel." The FTC is focused on a 2009 help center page, "We have now changed that page and taken steps to remove the ad cookies," Google said of the FTC charges. But more than the fine, this action indicates that regulators may be taking a more aggressive stance on the use of tracking cookies for behavioral targeting. Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WeJ9O3LVeTkS_5OR0iqBzio9cTviE9tUIwOzXZSieEVa8Oj4LF53Qf3lwEXcXSzssG0zKLFdPulZt-y3OEZLYIODTh72oxfPkFOFfvh9WTZly3upMEU199EjT4qgFPaISvazJjRYQE99Vn0HN4qaqrxsbF1oEZfjKDl1hnF2_pWkiAVasWwPC50GBGlNSvuxPSDk-gdczyBqaR-1IjWfCpcCO4CY8MpjD7fbGBVnO-M=>  


DirecTV's Sluggish Signal


The satellite TV provider's addressable ad plans <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WeJ9O3LVeTlKprSOo3NLQ6NJLaMfVd3mxNm5-6SSgHHP6o5y_J5guTA0tVtejfd0KpRH2SyUuzTNTWx9N4vpq3FNi-ohZ4i5GEAkfaSCAFHGKDr_UYHxuAdCYCbFRjav6ZIPJHnoHhEai0FodmXsCyT0eivaY20kDw6gVXD5Ggv125EDXUvwjunNNgAzP7NUONNZTSZbwHwmcHEFxXyAXTzZwyJa0qR12nB3C3hsKz5f-ywJR5f4og==>  are still taking a little more time than expected to come into focus. Multichannel News' Todd Spangler says <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WeJ9O3LVeTmxZLOWJZGLH5zjT0yOzySBbxBPuubZ6Cjoq2G7ww0AL2MXQw24boMdSrORuEjV55fr_kj7hA_kdaH1DhGiq0uhyfUhQUKssFKivIzJWgWR7x5DQ28LqLKWGiiNp15KsYEw8o_jMqUNK9JhewM34UIoGvTw15uFjZ_PVazO-J39q08EWfsOTmg1UaTaMVOFo-4=>  that DirecTV now says the national ad targeting features won't fully be rolled out until Q4, making it a year behind schedule. Everything appears to be in place: it's working with Starcom MediaVest Group on buys, Invidi on technology and with major marketers like Purina, Microsoft and Mercedes-Benz on the creative spots. It's not clear what the hold up is, but with all the challenges addressability faces, getting all the bugs out of the system will be necessary until marketers and agencies fully commit. 


Oracle Still Buying


On TechCrunch, John Constine covers the pending acquisition of social marketing tech company Involver and writes, "Involver will give Oracle a powerful toolset for helping brands create custom applications." Read more. No word on the price yet. This follows acquisition of Vitrue by Oracle and Buddy Media by Salesforce.com as data-driven enterprise solution providers grasp for social signal. The limited press release states, "nvolver's SML (social markup language) technology is expected to extend Oracle's social platform to help customers..." and read a bit more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WeJ9O3LVeTkLYNaHV1sGDr9m2I3MU5fUcKS_rxbjppG25lAbeaAx4wXQbezAOfzSrYBm9rJ93Nt0XziwDxo1fimbHeLKyHwYCRMi_0Rf122AEcwW2Y6AUTte2P-FDKuqCQMeh05L0h5J66iv1GMXalzvWyKeCXzwbLjgl0AT38Q=>  


Marketing The DSP


On YouTube, Kellogg's Bob Arnold's keynote address called "Why Ad Exchanges and Demand-Side Platforms Aren't Just for Direct Marketer" has been published on YouTube from MediaPost's recent Brand Marketers summit. Along the way, he provides a "programmatic branding recipe." See it now <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WeJ9O3LVeTkVtx2zFeO7c7N88bw0QqY6-tCtDfHfMdadh4bWzZKDINM0g1XrKgkyT8C680IYo1VXfgEaI-eCteTyoXztuhiH5gXOqh92aJG_fuo7m_PrM9cBeOk3gfEpSAksLh-lSoH07At-_Tun6w==> . 


Prospecting or Retargeting


A member of the Akamai Decision Solutions team (remember Acerno? <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WeJ9O3LVeTkA-eNR5kV79dB_7XbjpE8t_GfymM5R4h5Uy6JaciPiblGiNbACVSDldSxYPJ09CvRvjmpfulTdgfrfN1MhGYA_23krznbYAOqIUIGNwa3ZaidaYUDPVxPOslDtFnw0RqNfnoW0ZL-FMzD0p5CVUImgPFo2AlMlUBTmHdYRdtUx1njqvOiaHHC4> ), Avi Spivack, makes an appearance on the Akamai blog. He says, "Remarketing is a hot area of online ad technology, but if you're only using remarketing, you need to expand by including prospecting as part of your overall strategy. You cannot afford to rely on one solution; you need to keep customers and gain new ones." Akamai seems to be looking to fulfill the "prospecting" line item rather than bottom-of-the-funnel retargeting. Mapping the Yahoo Genome


Goodbye Interclick <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_Clc7JxWTAddeARyWm67puM7i99TjU61050glHKfT-byHYCOwOnkYAfiTSsoWO5C0yDSV1G8f_V6HYzszvnPqB0WSFsz2PMt7vEFZczokjoTOQ==> , hello Genome <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_Ck09FFeuFvFKqMrNcfLh5GUaryFwBre1uQIea8Q3VAQSLdPYdJgdmpWfUEHDQ3iLJHuv1bNUfsY1i_dVrvMLrvF6un_cVAG59N1I56Ym6nLjhOr1ZTD2Aob> . Yahoo has gone live with its integrated audience buying offering spawned <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_CnUDM6ZNvstJXS-vpPT8tt1gSz3zIyM6eW_oLbHn4VIHc0cSdE9w_uAlyxGDqPR2sJb7cqtzNOyNPLbw8bZM7GtNdBy_igKVzTMMuIbHiPP1Dss92aCiTz1Hk1N3tQsdRPT-7vtIq5jmNhSo-l3g5aEm-CpWQvRmRmM0_rvD-s2IK0wNb6fSwv46xGlTAgH5rtNLRyw0ogEMHlTfMaLXjHZ6A_vvSQ4RXU=>  from the purchase of Interclick late last year. The audience marketplace will bring to bear a range of first and third party data including Yahoo search and user data. As for inventory, that comes from Yahoo, the AOL/Microsoft deal, and Interclick's one thousand publisher sites. Peter Foster, Yahoo's GM of audience/performance advertising, calls Genome "a holistic combination of data inputs, premium supply and actionable analytics that can help marketers achieve their objectives from the top to the bottom of the funnel." Read the blog post.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_CnTWxXatawF8HGeN-RQrtcotNrzp9NR8khXt9tTFDXrTKN5uljU4oh5vJLSutVRcCaDgciN-76Nv-Kn45UK5TKuGCCBSnIC5CoWgigMA50s3tetLoT28vrk5rs-n82h0CXRZZdabP1_Bi6PB5pnAkHj6k07GoQEpNHSZyV9mL_P2sqh0gcMRpaNtcLrXisn-1_ls-6qXZTzAjk73ELLwYV6wP-t_ZjXMwInL0QqSEWP01nmwDsRdBeXqouVcZuyAAQ=> 


History Channel Demand Curve?


In the not-too-distant future, everything subscribable from newspapers to newspapers and magazines and cable will be available in a neat package for consumers. As anyone who's been watching magazine publishers grumble about acquiescing to Apple's "newsstand" policies, or seeing the slow adoption of TV Everywhere for cable operators, the big question is: will subscription-model media be able to generate sustainable revenue? Or will everything ultimately have to rely more heavily on an online ad model? Chris Dixon, angel investor and co-founder of eBay's Hunch, believes that "bundled pricing" can have benefits for buyers and sellers, particularly for popular cable TV channels. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_Cnor0Sx-3n8iAR88JXNQ-GmDkUiqxH9jCWISh2TeCt5IZRpia3eAVf_JYjFk4qI8ztUHLwwKgOjftanoUfVagID7jK0mQONFPU2fB77TTwPvVfgflfyUNUJECF84ByVzh0rSWUw47OpPB9XAX_uqwtZLhsDsWCn3wRt2GKyUKpIWQ6LRbKnZ6Vz>  


Display Dangers


Don't most analysts project continued double-digit growth for display advertising? Sure, much of that is going to Google and Facebook as they fight for display dominance. But surely there must be a lot to go around for the rest. Perhaps not, according to a Reuters report by Alistair Barr and Poornima Gupta, who look at the meaning of Microsoft's $6 billion writedown related to its purchase of digital ad shop aQuantive in 2007. "Ad industry executives say [Microsoft] might now join Yahoo in re-thinking its approach to Internet advertising, though there's no simple solution to the fundamental challenges they face," the Reuters duo writes. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_CnRzpJQIaNwp8rrg-h3CGEb_a08-ZA903pdlO1Y3zHbHfydhjitfJ4bxVtdf3wqxnUfCB2lqudkpsqGnwAZtf2I-Ocy6Ch37GJV4shrtAdONgQxwTumvUkqLYy_VwuyilHJ8hqfgnT1wyRm5nIAu3xYlDQOrp21CYQ5PIVPYRz9JQ==>  


Ad Tech Usability


In a world full of pretty apps, the ad tech arsenal has to embrace a design sensibility. Writing for Mediapost, Matt Stratz holds forth on how to "keep it simple," "understand color," and "add a showstopper," among other necessaries. "As consumer expectations for design migrate to business, it's more important than ever to build ad-tech systems that people actually want to use." Yield For Germany


Dirk Freytag has been hired by sell-side platform Rubicon Project to help with inventory efforts in Germany. A release states, "The former CEO of ADTECH and SVP at AOL (will be) working on a consultancy basis [to] increase the adoption and usage of the REVV real-time trading platform in Europe, manage the German operations and grow the local team." European RTB Report


London-based trading desk Infectious Media has released its Spring 2012 report on the European real-time bidding (RTB) market. According to the Infectious' data, "CPMs (cost-per-thousand) for advertising impressions in the UK are not the highest in Europe, with Italy and Germany now taking the lead. This shift has been led by relative price stability in the UK contrasting against rapid increases in Western European markets this quarter. These increases have also led to a strengthening of the East-West divide, clearly splitting the continent into two regions of relatively high and relatively low CPM. Scandinavia particularly saw CPM rise." Get the report (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_CmdyoJ98YtgI7lrH90aQ_vxSAbGK2t6fmjSVYQMw5Q2R7cbYG_GhL3Wxo-MMOf2KmeEEaPJt2jeU6MiNQp3LPQGB13aAa8Zj6XopF89tXidH6fUMINtBeiFKBrnnAk2Cqqc21sx96qdP_oPDsbanbC4r8jK-s2lmufzUDAuHCtnZ13CqLaOBqNu> . And, read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_ClnV6JFlcAtQFH1qN040y0-lzOTt40RXUgpwCciO8HVoiJtUedJiRI7tlad3xkVeW7M8_kP5_ooNQSq-pAGZxrpBUcMJND0dDWlzhZtKY2HXWpaFn3BheMswnhnZb7iTmtAs3lsYCOo0zU3FHibWVbXpbYFVOf2b5uXAXQtIRTgQLtIqRFUazEUhkkOtDlF3QdQbsysU--6TCL9EH6Q58hOdmtNPFd6Pz0SJ2x7rDS1bA==>  Infectious sees maturation in some countries when it comes to RTB <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015_NlTe0A_CkGaShIasjHpxNXHTbnMs4WR1N3ihgTvl3CiQe7HDqZivAFf3hm49iHgYmsctV0smze0GBFPRRjwDxABBOzPG4lhXuPB96Zor9IB1_5AfEWiGQPps57qAlvW6GEPq_tUwkjEQPpkCZQMvt2JS78NHUs6jntfjRyuzvaCNmi08aa0SFLPPEa3q4xp22xxtTL7z0=> , in others, high CPMs and presumably less exact pricing may indicate it's still early days.

Login Data And Ads


According to the Wall Street Journal, Facebook's plans a new type of mobile ad targeting that will leverage its own first party data. The WSJ sees radioactiivity, "The new ads could stoke privacy concerns because they let Facebook go a step further than mobile-ad networks, which track what ads people have clicked on through a phone's Web browser. Those networks aren't aware of all the apps that a user has on their phone." Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001zCTaa1TEMNQUHM7j8wZ_9g_erpjwQUjHfPUK-PrNbr8Kv2QQDnTfFYPkEdvoH6b5uZ9IRIpgfXq4YBvrJ6Wd8CVu5LiKM0Rt74fLp4SEnHVu2sFwgZrUn7Szg-DnGK-bh-wv8I3dRIT4jUFLfeSogqoY3YRenvrMaA4bxv3PgGsI_6hkzReQR48aSQ1-WTiN>  That's the key difference between what a third-party ad network can do versus first-party publisher data in mobile where the use of user data is often agreed to by the user when they sign up for the publisher (Facebook in this case).


Aussie Exchanges


In an interview in Australian Financial Review,  Mi9's GM for Microsoft's Media Network and Advertising Exchange, Marc Barnett, is unequivocal when discussing who the big players will be in the future: "We believe that long-term, there will only be two exchanges in this market: ours and Google's. Our point of differentiation will be that we provide premium-brand, safe environments that offer an alternative to the long-tail sites Google aggregates in their offering." Microsoft is saying to audience buyers that context matters. Read more on AFR. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001zCTaa1TEMNTj3qaRb4lmj1qzMXg8_sG_wW_awRtGW4H3zr38xP5xpVWh8gumWdkreWyFs-4afsGhh6SkTrFfCS_z1H1ybvXGEytncF9vlV73UZ0Grd2CZnrGIKWi1CMLq2god6v1IcAnFBWOTBRPkPM94ENXd5BDkQAqb3oq98gNFdt_yFHDXH_6WORY4Cil8EA395YKjNv3LeMPHpOeQVqfvW-Zzvow>  Mi9 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001zCTaa1TEMNQKaYEPiAM803wpSEhaPcIZFMi935uj-SIMNpeYo4vJ5ji6OdIhkts9az85XlVc9iSrOzbcBbqH2IbJeli9hSkPSYeRjmM3jd_pUMmINHGAJeWnV8z7Zhu1zu6obCbDYeA=>  is a joint venture between Microsoft and Nine Entertainment in Australia.


Facebook Lends 'Likes' to Yahoo?


Here's a big win for Yahoo advertising, if it's true. AllThingsD's Kara Swisher reports that Facebook and the purple people eater have verbally agreed to bury the hatchet on patent legislation initiated earlier this year by Yahoo's former CEO Scott Thompson. As part of the ceasefire the two will work more closely on content and ads. Importantly, Yahoo may be the first outside site to receive FB "like" data for use in its own display advertising. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001zCTaa1TEMNSoj7zHRRycf-60BMz1J5RGzW-dt1g9wxC4AKGQ9RdlS-4s8EiriX60det72y-kOgfirS2K4NoNuryOTPUrnlwipdfJ2AE7MRPcL1QTDaMu7fwGBQwdDLvEtT0yLvHjZoFu-R2wsS7FbhMKnFNQHN54TiRkGijK50eCPY97gwoLJdfFPChC96tsmZBcp_dMl94SHc9RfsvTN1OZrF1QZs5DuyV9eknBJaW2Aw_ASXyCGg==>  If it comes to fruition, the pact will mark the second time Facebook has armed a Google adversary with social graph data, having already boosted Bing <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001zCTaa1TEMNTmDqbNcLrh7qIr5VqTRIgcVMfJUoqA5KYO5ljAlJ5jjKWoD2Hqqhx-YPSRebxDiR7H1cETJg1ptPzYWpZwSbKbcis8j67XMiSGm1_W0raJrGa32-kyGhKjVGkFhAfuLre-wvypWaGPhz2R21oSuRkX6JAZ_S8k24kFJXvfdNenvdfEqe9zWJjV>  with friend data. 


Local Ads Heat


Local ads 'plumbing' provider Yext is profiled by hyperlocal trade pub StreetFight which says Yext's recent $27 million capital raise was done at an impressive $270 million valuation. The investment community is hot for the local ads/marketing solution Holy Grail. StreetFight says "that as the market shifts towards discovery and away from traditional local SEO, services that solve information problems within the discovery/search ecosystem (like fragmentation) will see substantial growth." Read a bit more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001zCTaa1TEMNQATYEVfm1Zt8HHU6Nas8nj0aKGj2X0bIoVc946h3BXoxulzYuJDkcTgaNisinSx9jlCBGKrARjNcSTHyQG5Txtc6pEnIC40ltozZaanmDhhswKz-ptdXlB17gGsT4pcy-n1498LN6AnL18yqc9wdFbfCqU8YW2pzMekfnG0Ox9uTICchYbqDYtJ5zX_d0ymrQrEiEOEGrAec49a-2qw4Z4PBdUe9LTXhE=>  


Stuffing The Cookie


A new "affiliate cookie stuffing" whitepaper has been published by attribution company Convertro which says that the practice of trying to be the last cookie standing when a consumer makes a purchase is a game many are playing. "If online marketers are utilizing last click attribution model cookie stuffers are the biggest attribution winner. When looking at the prior click (before the cookie stuffing) we see that other affiliates are impacted more than any other channel (32%); that is to say, cookies stuffers take away credit from other affiliates using a last click attribution model." Hence, the need for anything other than last click attribution. Get it (pay with some PII). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001zCTaa1TEMNQhlI3iOM3FWYz2SMQ1_NLHmaP8YLfwk74nwjRnZRVLJQcSJpKy7FKBC1sko2ADGFQDb2pyFRSNXu9CrU3bwL2jT-HgkiCjNHH3xH8OpX3Ici0_IAled4iq0FnDZOoUuFQBcLaql0YgRMuUPpwVNFYSvYGSXRG0gJ8S38E-kM6WRw==>

Yahoo! CEO Race


Yahoo! interim CEO Ross Levinsohn and Hulu CEO Jason Kilar are in the lead to be the permanent CEO of Yahoo! says Yahoo! 'insider' Kara Swisher on All Things D. She writes, "At this point, said sources, it appears to still be a situation that is Levinsohn's to lose. Along with having been at Yahoo for several years, the media-savvy exec has also recently scored points with the hiring of a new and very well-regarded sales chief Michael Barrett. In addition, some Yahoo board members feel that adding yet another new CEO into the mix from outside could further destabilize a company that has gone through the leadership wringer over the last year." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmD8kaEBo03URmCrNCWgAw3-kQW-6v4xFQbJAZ7a8FSIij-Cn3jKZspbQFuEiO2NmwAspsnMRgN-tCYn51wfyq95LPPIsZOhE5bmBNuykIcBVn0PynSkKHGmJ95_4ZNSW0eVYfRQxvbKnCCn_HtZ09VRjajSW7rDLPKgdL9Lb4csMmY16FlbuT2C26_XTYg1foYTycDOQIGvvQ==>  


Rivalry: Facebook's API and DSP Partners


Is the race to "own" the Facebok ad channel a jump ball between demand side platforms and Facebook's API partners? David Williams, CEO of Blinq Media (a Facebok API partner), tackles the question in an AdAge column. "Ad API partners can still help brands and agencies target based on first-party data, while the FBX is restricted to cookie data - a major limitation." He also argues the Ads API program is about brand while FBX is a DR vehicle. So the keyword is "complementary." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmDcxs0iL8xQy16x1JcF_h0mUxzdkio5jdj-J_Sj82szIgkoupOx0ftPRaEt0lXfYkuhPfDPB3AO51BzvySIRWLVEh3AEeoejAAo5sJC9WK_CyKGQHDpZ9C0LVXfIuiU6wB08wX2Co4J5OJ-CVaFewtaCwSmbYkx6paW_FfFR_5ieak_0Zz-fvWTpn9oJLupPzduoxfeFA5hRQ==>  


Sales Call Culture


Upstream Group's Doug Weaver sees negativity wafting from the 'sales call culture' of the digital seller. He admonishes sellers to keep their heads up and don't fall into any traps - the client needs you. Here is a sample tip: "Too many sales people still don't listen to understand. Instead they're simply thinking about the next point they'll make or the next detailed follow up question they'll ask. Active listening is the cornerstone of a great meeting, but it's not something that just happens. You may be born with it, but unless it's stressed and nurtured, it soon fades away." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmAJCrLMQgNr4A_FZ93PsAbeBDpJ4vi_zetw3seae7iyne2urL-rsh7Z5rUnIyt7BCIxD2ZacygTcAEZvIlF4Kpmhc6-x9ieJgNPE0GyZ5Jys3XL-uRs3CGWVyS7yhQ4enNf7yJFWlEhrQ==>  


Cross-Channelling


Mobile ad targeting firm Media Armor announced that it has partnered with tag management platform BrightTag. BrightTag's blog says this will open up cross-channel remarketing and "illuminate post-impression conversions and engagement cross-channel." There's more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmDqNpeV1OUEL9PxcrZQ-O5lyNJI3xaBezb9fhsIyRLj_ZfqKSCRNHSmnkCIipUlaRGoKaP3YrzeKdYGMCQDPZQXfEQbx-jEzY6gFstrsb5kS1ppns_j1-IfczlkhcjA-__fUToU_kcrKvhrWt7lKV_eSubcNuF5RobZmwOVb0P68a-GrDDcehV4082ahHFBewc=>  Clients want efficient cross-channel buying - whether they know it, right now, or not. 


Location Rules


Amazon made it official and acquired 3D mapping company UpNext which makes local maps similar to what you see in games such as "Grand Theft Auto" says Wired. Read a bit more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmBIOBEpvGAxICzaThugMwH0IWxrlEnFMNPnq47vEPN5uzBE_jNggB7WRY1fLfq9zEXfhJhO5rjjPuzgK5i85MpfDwskgYHCA5Um5JWmX4cwGyMpF_hZuT2XG6D-db2RiJz_OPEYG62y-pLatPKzUy5tUBRSL6kXu7zJ1BMAZdhbWlJv2Zpvosdp> . Though not explicit in the announcement, virtual reality advertising (remember Massive? <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmCz-Ha73Pe58Kq3mZnkZna00i_lNRCH1Bmwxgilc9gwexQbTTGA64-0ky-YI7WSwlZhmWndRGVQkmxClUeqv13Tj0gn45uCPZcFljtpPWD8jxesrKCUU1bGVNqO3hv5kOEhzOLhW3YCJw==> ) could be making a comeback through your favorite mapping software - yet another wrinkle for local ads, let alone local commerce. More from GigaOm. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmCNshU-_iXDUn3IuqvNXL7JxMrUnRBQLhgDq2sx-taR4l_Cbe1sgicd3Q1PR7DOujn_baf8e065XRRHeU8CvN8ualGRT6-DZvJwoNfNRcFLN8MGI9dWgGraLgZqMS1MBvEyzePkQw5V71ZJzangOvaQwPboxtUeQ4NsMe1teRRqbEe6VGk4fGl_>  


Make My Data


In a new whitepaper from [x+1], the company explores the data management platform (which also [x+1] offers) and sees the confluence of four disruptors that marketers can address with the DMP: digitization of media, mobile, digital payment systems and social media. Download it to learn more (pay with some PII) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JfH4q-mKNmCBkzgATvFhwUHQ6Q2OEZHfizlLApInp2E-8U9QzCa8tjNSLlgvyGUpJbAx9THcn-pAxPFGlnfmz0rSKhQBKHaEkIhR2DbzyR42RFRPS59LQWRdTMgv9vJUvvyCbPS-Dhw=> .

*	GroupM: Programmatic Surges in UK, As Facebook Ad Growth Slows <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnZMn-PKTNVAeEyaL_ozJXaGhIy7cuCvPpcvRpfaeI9zPOIIP1VW8wU7v3WyhUfegCFuqZBe_izHe_0kCLd36eQcT6z273T0S4pvmZrUnnPOLGds1BKwBhmub9UIxW02T4fUNb-CwvUd8j9HwS5a7vkKjuWl-QGcRoKT8vndUaNGSYOuA9ckJc7kMKhH5trUI3bwvkec-TprsqKut1qXeYI3>  "We're seeing a marked slowdown in our billings growth with Facebook. I think Facebook's long tail business is probably doing very well, but the large advertisers [are growing less quickly]. We think one of the serious constraints is thinking within the client organization on how we formulate Facebook strategy. Facebook marketing is so universal; it effects so many parts of a client's business. You need an integrated approach to managing this. That is the problem -- getting everyone around the table." (visit AdExchanger.com)

Mo' Money Mobile


It's a 'funding-a-day' in ad tech! On Tuesday, mobile app marketing platform Fiksu announced it has added $10 million ($17.8 mil total) in new funds to its coffers. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnYTnNX3WJepDf1oOTeFbCjPkfU3PtI66N14kSaG8HYczcPdEeLHMgPcOiVWFQ5dSFuyb13rFD_0L9oRBAd8D9ZmeBmLq_T0K8VTY4ka7iBZN9rbRVhzscaNdd9dSwPFbwRiESsPNNa8FeF6YT8ToHBoiz0BGIiQQ99uyM8zsk4tYzi4Orc5QHB6ZxXHA4QbN63AkLCloHxKuKjYpNE6c2tGSBB6jbMUFFkVl4qvoDumhB9I2CnftqpjJNHZSqP9MH5HGlas5hdOb5TH0GUrku73yP6rNKP_b-9eNi9_R__thw==>  - which gives a pretty good sense of how Fiksu plans to differentiate itself as it heads off into European and APAC markets. Also of note: mobile device company Qualcomm is putting its venture arm's funds to work in Fiksu. The lines are blurring between devices, telecom and ad tech products and services. Read the Feb. '12 AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnb8z5rc4Au3quySnECgJ_3HwgQ3yiWY0cQS77x3lXKhFvw3NCVRuT1CLhd3lPM2eHDAGEG7TBNH_YFWmMqWinsKeiRjbDhBmi07KZ-Aix4BDLCJ5fB9EDewcNGhfSvhuxs=> &A with Fiksu CEO Micah Adler. 


Airtight Frequency Caps


In a post on the FTC's tech blog, the agency's CTO Ed Felton suggests methods of frequency capping that are more privacy-friendly than storing ad and website data linked to third party cookies. One of these pitches server-side cryptography to mask userIDs. "Rather than using the pseudonymous userID as a key for storing and retrieving the frequency counts, the ad network can hash the userID together with the advertiser's campaignID and use the resulting value as the storage key." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnY4qTVwb753E8tG1AGCDcMlhm6PQX7l7VlRYPEhRuyAIzHvvEX6Rt7IC5dyFpH1M-u79i7jGCupmzOOf6BZPrTHm_RLEBrZ2RQsv9LlIqDYYqVYY4YehTBT6tfQ3OO95Qvx9-V3ORrO1OBuBX9KoNAdU-UH_sGWBc6omHlajB1IcKd0t-c-ZurjLWOCzmCjo60=>  


Google-Verified Ads


Is Google trying to drink the ad verification milkshake? A birdie tells AdWeek's Tim Peterson that the company is baking the capability into the DFA suite and may roll it out by end of summer. DoubleVerify CEO Oren Netzer offers this positive spin: "It's our belief that every impression is going to be verified in the near future, whether it's two or three years down the road. Google releasing a product is a big testament to that." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnZA_uvlPJV9TVuhGivUmeCyoKTF4WuSBywKkqhgi7PS-znBhnRALTckCvGfsTh4JzXwtTDgP7GJ8m3G2uGcp0hJKRAd-J45YbgJ_-W8_cFtiQhJpCYU-PHF6bagxUOFpqoV7mP_lCUWgYd-amlZaxGn-Rw1vYtsMT1gM9laUDdP4AYFiXgiz1cqsVsZo3mIeukYiHHVY8lbxQ==>  


GM's Facebook Ads


The Wall Street Journal reports (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnaq2ocrPRtXKKPP-n9wE9S8L4nu9kaIAhE7khoW25S7t-Y_IzxCN1hVL0RsKQMt-XOrEL3i6fM_CvwN71EJOfckyRR-W2kJ6cDWvt85jlZVALFftr0HYwqDkBqkwkCzcJAcI6yy2K-ubSOO1e11v4-MGV_Hr6GIxr_oxrTu07ZeTzs2uGoqHG9->  that General Motors is "in talks" to have GM advertise through Facebook paid ads again after GM famously said that it would not do so just as Facebook's IPO was underway. Reuters adds, "Although the two companies remain far from reaching an agreement, Facebook executives have assiduously courted the world's largest carmaker. One source said Facebook was not pushing for GM's immediate return, but offered to provide data showing the effectiveness of [Facebook's] paid ads." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnYHDoBGsQ6o3s0U_LrElVEo8AmeNcmoFAOnb2xLiEZgorh4_-5PEbHDEtySKT6bSq2-0dv509TsLPErr_Kg8-U2iiQ0PR7uVUrDO7HGwh5eQDiRvA4265RubK9j2t9R3OFoSS5BgnZwcqBNhbGumNB-pOTRk4LZI9KPMxtrTP5iaLou0QlnALmtrRyYIwmNXLpAzccD5lwtMbqr8zhhy9s8DnAkFnCGgTMorMexGT-so0hL9uy5MzWdvfR0zan__Z3lIVZgeMvMq9-yJUauSNbANgIaxby6Wwp4SbJJJBPBKgy-luT1b_Pu>  


Buy Or Hold?


Interpublic Group was one of the earliest marketing services companies to recognize the potential of Facebook, investing a relatively small $5 million in the social network in 2006. There appears to be a dispute over how much the ad holding company has benefited from that stake. Mediapost's Joe Mandese <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnYuxwEC7xk5EO_tBCTLuRR8_PAbICTBWdEYj0sin949cAVPVGB3fxjwUi4zIl8BDOB3Kzih3T-e7q6nrxm3xKGq6Q2YTI4HEg7hTt0Ydfb5z7XDedZb3SMLk7o52HqroU0xBDNmtEhMw6ghPl5FZJ0Gz8-FbAIVjB00KMqA4LduGScSxwKqCmTtGIByD-Lx2be3Yh0xfi-o8NjM-7BVM0MKVeuUgjHzp4A=>  reports that IPG is denying a claim made in former executive's suit that it sold the remainder of its shares in Facebook following the social network's initial public offering in May. The executive, Ray Volpe, says he deserves about $381 million from IPG helping steer the company to make the 2006 investment. 


Always On Display And Facebook


On ExchangeWire, Wayne Blodwell of Universal McCann argues that display is an Always On channel, "We're at the point now where everyone understands that in the world where display needs to perform on a last-click basis that retargeting is the most successful strategy (rightly or wrongly). If an advertiser were to remain 'Always On' through the year, they would be able to grow the retargeting cookie pool consistently by finding new users with their prospecting strategies, and retarget them..." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnbbI2Ncan0ljHC5RTWkrSMCOlfddl13j4Igf8sFYvfR9kZSTG0ZXnYaEEC7tx__S-3iXaHn0SxKsGKwRK4zrOQQc1nZu0X_CxdWSQr34Ru_wQ0c3Gx36nsXvLVXDY-CVj4wHZLxleRpjsw3zHxEJeOl5AfyyS3-Wu3-M9YWLfPC3vzNXX3sOcbvLmKIYk-3bx_JvR96OS2H-A==> . Meanwhile on AdMonsters, Adaptly CEO Nikhil Sethi argues Facebook should be "always on," too: "The overarching power of Facebook lies not just in the pure ability to serve a highly targeted impression to an individual, but also to retain that person within a social environment and communicate with them on a consistent, 'Always On' basis via rich, compelling content." Read that one <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k9iovCvCrnbgAhqflbGTo3biE2Dno4RVA1oA7OEOEw4BhYD6KO_ehJpaUVHoSErMPcByKWya2NEC0kpO4qw8cN6g5XW1nWJOu2lEk9nxZxQFnUbMKfqDHmzwCm_TFSTw1DGRj5SHl7gtyByFBu-7FBFpnwvIT6Xo> .

Uncapture The Flag


Microsoft has had enough, fiscally, of its aQuantive acquisition. As you may recall, it was the largest of a series of digital media acquisitions that year which included Google buying DoubleClick, Yahoo buying Right Media, WPP buying 24/7 and even Microsoft buying comparatively tiny AdECN. From the release yesterday, "Microsoft completed its acquisition of aQuantive on Aug. 13, 2007, in an all-cash transaction valued at just over $6.3 billion. While the aQuantive acquisition continues to provide tools for Microsoft's online advertising efforts, the acquisition did not accelerate growth to the degree anticipated, contributing to the write down." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSYJVOmhyMhiaO4QMKm0hW4HeCEBMMzhP-HT0BQWHussFwMWlVxHKsW7ONR72Nmhic6vfyBkQSqAi9mZ7FIYaRHKlCbFOdNrWWVfwbOrDEynHbrd3GSck_KtrqzE7gI43O-ljOqh_06HUgrU79LVcUUGlm-bozlXitxVHaCx0di1VxN2sfpO3dDBZJYNIf-CeNae4YdylQaa3kL5miLw_kZ6>  It hasn't all been a loss though. In its 2009 deal with Publicis, Microsoft sold Razorfish, which had been part of aQuantive, for a reported $530 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSax0XbWvkzbtaNU-gxJYJuQhyDhmXXjL9Fny6QGKh2Tos4l4ret8HlGSusW-kP5aEC5jh0mzhVC_suhvaEIxZ8nZvmLnhsV8SzJfvZQYZcpNBJpBuiGgVAD7W7xsWarRjjJfASZxO9uwVM2dRKdnzZahpGsG6gc2Rixsiu1A83nkusXr7uA5YzIUs3SrB9tGeA=> .


Mobile $$$


Mobile ad network Jumtap has dipped into the stream of venture capitalness and added another $27.5 million in new funding. That's $121.5 million raised since 2005 according to Crunchbase <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSYLvcOyCS5uhK-RXnfABxT-DMOCTx1W_3aDMpl7-vPihlJpP9Xv6uvg967mGwwUqcLyoHpOBFgcqHOeMjLJ-fmaHPC-vKIDMJxc4UzzesX6AsBQPJdDyeOTGIOOEfCCWMk=> . The release gives some sense of scale, "Each month Jumptap reaches 107 million mobile users in the U.S. and 156 million mobile users worldwide, and delivers 20 billion mobile impressions. The Company has also experienced a surge in the development of its technology patent portfolio, with 29 patents issued and 200 pending. To support its escalation, Jumptap has grown its employee base by 50 percent in 2011." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSaUNXymGkmSM6Yg7v3vMW4o9GlBZH7E7nZsA_dQFjuFcuqUQb-rhqTpzMJdOpFk4MeJPLnoiOBqyTKiP2wODmne_YHLYodH_HoARO4x5URAaOadhM0sbA0eHYqIEvIJwXbZsFzZNMmbfWYglI41_pWWBso0i_vspDU4R5ryOiGoenX_AT0H8thI3yUxRfx_pRvGrLeBIo2Jtl7HaBONXRzfBKe2AfvJUi5jq53yyGFPtw==>  


Answering Ask's Ad Question


Ask.com's <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSarFhK3h55ntDRiiBVdkxhe-9FAJ4FckjL2IF-pwx4fVoA9Iy70UecJqdGwqzb0dlKK3wCVIH2cb04U6LGPpPHQtRtuiZDqzuU=>  acquisition of content discovery provider nRelate <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSarFhK3h55ntDRiiBVdkxhe-9FAJ4FckjL2IF-pwx4fVoA9Iy70UecJqdGwqzb0dlKK3wCVIH2cb04U6LGPpPHQtRtuiZDqzuU=>  could help the IAC-owned Q&A site get back into the ad game on its own terms. Since 2007, Ask has outsourced search ad sales to Google, while it has concentrated on differentiating itself as human-driven seek-and-respond site, as opposed to relying on algorithms. While the company will not be building up a sales team, Ask CEO Doug Leeds told AdExchanger, "We see what nRelate does is extend the native ad formats associated with search. In this case, nRelate has relationships with tens of thousands of publishers. So as we attempt to connect users with content, we'll also be better able to send them contextually relevant advertising." More details on Ask's blog. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSb2STBYshZhi0WpSd3bw91TvXEeIQZqg65SzClfUU7jzAzqWkJMRHw4BkUZ2Bejxvihtw1h0lEqfc4IwjsbPJm3Y--0Zocwsd6LYAuMfn1RhorKism2_2w9Fe7MI1mFw8mLyU2MqvRJ9WdGDGnD6WRv7Zym6TLw6s4=>

Owning Brands


OwnerIQ has nabbed $7.5 million to execute on its promise of "ownership targeted media." (press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSaQV6CJY-7GAOBtLVgYphE-oiIMMrJAtrs4qINwKaYNM0mU3Z_F7nJIR-Rczzn6TAokYrdnL7NR15g6y4KklxLBdtImHzflwHH8l35n9ZzjOhULrBsLQ3dKA-Wh0DRN_0HpeaRf0alG6ipba-Hxb3_a> ) Early on the company offered a destination site for digitized product manuals, with accessories and "after market" brands in mind as target customers. Since then it has pivoted slightly to focus on targeting in-market consumers as well. AdAge picks up the story: "OwnerIQ will serve up co-branded ads to people that have visited, say, an audio speaker-maker's website that attempt to drive that shopper to an e-commerce site where they can buy the speaker." Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSYqa3tOVzzeG15mH-05oPGjhQSv-Qo5TB3xmjSLzmEtn85aITAzetYc-fgLJpDpdAdcREbo2_wa0uc661FC_rjsEwdW5YuMwsWde4qQdExwu6jrSjPwnBx0getwHWmYvaol13pTfE_n_evUCV4f1ZP8blpoJ_YPJ21yBifDlyf9e4tYZZvf9ai_Bz0I4_mfJ0tiA34PtQCnFQ==> 


FBX Origin Story?


Writing on his blog, Jay Weintraub speculates on how Facebook execs might have arrived at the idea of a private exchange model built to capture retargeting dollars. He imagines one saying, "Other ad networks couldn't do this because they might have a large aggregate reach but not the frequency. Our users go on and off the site all the time... We enable others to retarget their users on our inventory. We become our own exchange. Targeting problem solved. Monetization improves dramatically." Read the post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001efPIEitKtSb_rtCWbkWooOkdYZCf9K_TNlalJ6pUmLQ9V-gi2ISf0PwifNMtLHe24GrudSzbsJK3wCS57bPI5CM8wGQz8-nUf9NSvUk_HDdckzWot2WFor5lvDrQC8NZRk51q8nE2Nobb8uITWF6QwAASf-EZP_sft_ODNJJ-Uhx4GqzQ5KKBYZuKxHI5OVdZwyGQK0zQb400eJB7knKwg==>

Scrubbed Of Tweets


LinkedIn is getting back some of its screen real estate as it said Friday that tweets will no longer be displayed on the B2B network site. A LinkedIn email to users explains, "LinkedIn and Twitter have worked together since 2009 to enable you to share your professional conversations on both platforms. Twitter recently evolved its strategy and this will result in a change to the way Tweets appear in third-party applications. Starting today Tweets will no longer be displayed on LinkedIn." Read a tiny bit more in a freshly updated LinkedIn FAQ. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8J7vlNZSVMW9s3TpPLtwpgVZfmxeDxsBO0nLsPgtQJeYMe2yj1MQ4lPeNEcsaopfF0JH-RJe6vyJalaywPzzu3dD73stMLib6ZYc3Uc0HoHPtgs_6DXa9UbkoJoD2oatKqZqSeE_0okmCf22hQePP5RYBRsugZKtfw=>  The reason: Twitter is taking back the tweet "experience" to its products and services. Read the blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8Jse3V7WjzeF1bbq6JMnGwfu3b_0i3vjYyostKHr2dqBGcZYThrpGyk9B8G3F4u-0UaWGBENzFCf6F7fc0igU8HAXnOxqnVj_bYXNih4wwBFbEcgU6I_H07Ssa7qETyJdtYgHFw7WJwuxytjjiqF2TkipLdEFvv-CDPw35US04fwA==>  But, is it about "experience," or - data leakage <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8LwOfgHo2L5h4sPWe53_LfWvsTYLhnMG6QxV_0OwXssET01lNhiH7oZ_uCpZF3u4P0ADARvs2S9LtG2jUe9d2tR7ei1U-Gxb9lB1qX7omKEWH_nNtKK4nHXthQ3SnoSMSHfBrlR6jVGznIc3y4-IkicCc6cfeBBlgo=> ? 


Yahoo! Displayland


Peter Kafka works through some scenarios on Yahoo!'s ad tech plans on All Things D. His sources tell him that deals won't get done until Ross Levinsohn (or someone else) is in place as the permanent CEO. But, it's possible that tier 1 and tier 2 display ads could be addressed with Google Doubleclick technology. PubMatic and AppNexus are also in the mix. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8KC2hqjPSif9QUo-eRDwumnmr2vA2i_SDzfIWf3Fi5zqpYtfZCjzfB3Am941toHmhdXERwn_vZxtV1BB43GLObqdghZtDat2Ohkqh8c0EqB7JqxAtHtF4RYCHwH_NRsNi8YvxQt5lyN_ccGPLwlywx1M_wypdQ67P9_1-LG905pnoPKn79qpNxJ51HAr1RwzrY=> . Adweek says Rubicon Project is, too. Read that one. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8JVyGwq-sbk6HB1-420VY6lOUi5DCsn-I424Ovwt6fn8wZMdF5IITH5msKTyTvIJXirXKXAaxlipO_wu7iv8o7ujBmkhy8j_ua71Pp1FnM2SWUB_MpLiQhHXSZ4FAy7mp31OZnW7Vf9mhzcGYgj0IGqUJnWNzZM1akKWP83l2b5P438IKZ4wa8k3UHQ4_3DYjCkDjlUP9wlEpP82j6Sp3mW>  


In Favor Of Facebook Ads


The media battle rages as to whether or not Facebook ads work. This time, Zappos 'Facebook marketing lead' Nate Luman checks in on Digiday and says, "We've spent about $10 million over the past two years at about a 3.5:1 ROI. About 99 percent of that spend has gone toward direct-response ads driving traffic to Zappos.com. (...) when we consider where Facebook ads fall in the sales funnel and compare them to similar marketing efforts (mainly category-head search terms), they deliver similar performance, fuel other channels (drive long-tail search and comparison-shopping queries), and are one of our best marketing channels for driving new customers." Another for the "yes" column. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8Iiyl0nGjbvd8KCPQHN91i2SJfJnFnEm2cfQJs6P4Bb_lY1-PoKQRPretcSsCTWD5xsfu1jR18_L-O6GuH31zY8Lw1E2rZW0w9KrA7o1nm7W6nodHmQH31_NEMTR4b5bY946ExR13gOJgDZTB0ADrbHRQDHfGzRjelmXZq7aOkL4OVtkZnmlt3Y> 


Addressing Viewability


GfK, the Germany-based company that bought Knowledge Networks last year <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8KdJ9bjGbktTaqv2t7ejD5ArXL1GIA-MdWP6w-8hk8Tmc2mZnxLTp--P3HTpVxyu5gZ5bElh890PeVTZ0KGhE6BfPICNeY03PXXTjqH3Ea-arD-MS4HSdsayGjU2JW4tG0ZRuyr0es6b0ccCSF7GUNkrHWHnt0Tvs8=> , is offering its solution to the viewable impression <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8Kd4Vke8Bf--T-9090UQgy0H5T1aijWctFngW3izaBOgHv1BwI5nzsmiYxKqniAKE1S2ukci2WVE76toK2BZUV_V8KU1NfDhKc4i4CsIfUpyRK2abhFUG3SF0x0PMLUNLQOgW6Kr8jTSqC-MmRT2gLIJbqkBEXJ--M=>  dilemma. From the release, "DeliveryControl.dx tracks browser activity (browser window or active tab), the position of the advertisement on the website, the user's screen resolution, and any scrolling by the user. The reporting displays the different levels of visibility of the advertisement - whether it was fully displayed (100%) or if at least 90%, 75%, 50% or 1% were visible on the user's screen - and the average view time for each of these visibility levels..." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8Ku2WjTv5n9QTXalvpOfHJZnchfQ5MaBWxDQVW7g4MUxduav9BeVtYezsaitF1VTtmMAcbC5XmxB69ElZQl2JU252l8B9bObVrwFKV8gjO19MnmQqkOrzM0Upd1Rcl5JX9ZbeLpGYnWtbMQfYxg-CqFhX5ujEp4qlLHfVpgzgZ7maMmzavb3XZSgcAWMl_TtXU=>  


The Seven Secrets


AdMonsters republishes a piece by BrightTag SVP of Partner Development Todd Chu called "Seven Secrets of Highly Successful Vendors." He believes investing in data collection 'talent' and the development of a data collection API is a good start. About the latter, he writes, "In most cases, the tracking tag is just a lightweight API that uses a cookie to establish a user ID and collect some data. In the past, these tracking tags were very limited in scope, because they were implemented on small numbers of pages and collected little data." And now... <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8LD_9MDd5ffYkGCJu6xVHtMd80DXoQNgUJ9R6OTLC4v7H1eQ81g6AY1qKl5X9E98_mbNnZSWgmeuf4xA9aVsC30y5LntZDglMzJuKaMGBTei1k__wD8vDBn942IJCxX9OgmJ0S3hnRc_iVErPblkhAKyXK0_clr_860B_groye6dQ==>  


Aol Reorg


Aol is making internal moves as the content, ads and "membership" biz are being put in different silos. TechCrunch's Ingrid Lunden covers the news and sees ad tech, "Advertising.com, will be an interesting one to watch. This is the space where AOL is pinning a lot of hope for revenue growth - online ads not just on its own properties but throughout the web - but it's also hugely challenged with players like Google and Facebook commanding huge leads on overall online ad revenue share." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8JE8YFVihzoGA58C4rRCe8g63UlxlnBtneNbWKZZZK7P1gEufw7JeG7ncVfG2HgB1u_BtfVEIkQ60ZxWSBfZtqo7zcrgBCaZJGDuJ4_zBmzPiqwYBVphtSRhqcUDyeYi6Tt4usqVlGzct4Ufli66YKfRUbs0p1zoIUOnTZmxoxxBWrAm6NnKCpgsZFmBJLLJ5J_pjGeiYbEm3osHCyvvrptFtctyaA9fH0=> 

 
The End Of Offline Retail


On his blog, Jeff Jordan, a VC at Andreesen Horowitz, makes his best case for why offline retailers will be crushed by online retailers. The refrain is familiar but the detailed proof is more compelling as Jordan believes the trend will feed on itself, "Online retail will benefit greatly from the elimination of their physical competition and their growth should accelerate." And, we'll never go outside again. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czdM0Jldy8IrLCEjBmcp16yKqu8Sn_ZXWici1N02cfJ_giG12x9xKKsgpHeCEpkxjS-qB9_yvA1DeX0BcNCai1yqjUAEBaAAq3GQyhhgRqVmdA5lvWaVPIMtX4oPw60VhKuUyNSJIRadZiPpKHiZTeyyCgMxx0HmXoTLnKrhltBGT4Bwt6SQwuiuTQu_J7E4Qmd23IN3oe4=>  There's too much innovation going on to let all brick-and-mortar retailers slip into oblivion.  And, offline, in-store data is unique and valuable.
